|     | \*\*Arthur Schopenhauer\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | \*"Life swings like a pendulum backward and forward between pain and boredom."\* / \*"The world is my representation... \[its inner nature is\] Will... a blind, incessant impulse..."\* / \*"Aftre after all, death is the result of life."\* / \*"Suicide, far from being a denial of the will to live, is one ofits strongest affirmations."\* | Worldly (Cosmic Pessimism / Revelation of Blind Will as Suffering / Inherent Futility) & Transcendent (Aesthetic Contemplation as Temporary Escape / Ascetic Denial of Will as Path to Nothingness/Nirvana) | Schopenhauer’s nihilistic event is the \*\*philosophical unveiling of the noumenal reality as a blind, striving, and inherently painful Cosmic Will,\*\* with the phenomenal world (our representation) being its ceaseless, tormented objectification. "Pain and boredom" are not accidental states but the very rhythm of this Will-driven existence. Life's ultimate ground is not rational or good, but an irrational, unfulfillable striving that \*is\* suffering. Death is the inevitable, mundane end, but suicide offers no true metaphysical escape, as it affirms the very Will-to-Live that causes suffering. This realization of universal, ontologically rooted suffering is the core rupture, exposing the groundlessness of all optimistic or teleological worldviews. | \*\*Ignorance (Will as Noumenon):\*\* His concept of the Will is often simplified to mere psychological drive or "life force," rather than grasped as the fundamental, pre-individual metaphysical principle of all reality, the irrational Ding-an-sich behind all phenomena. The \*cosmic scope\* of its inherent suffering is thereby reduced. \<br\> \*\*Ignorance (Pessimism as Temperament):\*\* Interpreted as merely the product of his personal melancholy or a curmudgeonly disposition, rather than a rigorously argued philosophical system deducing pessimism from metaphysical first principles and empirical observation. The "pain and boredom" are seen as subjective feelings, not ontological states. | \*\*Displacement (Aesthetic Contemplation):\*\* Art is often seen as a simple "pleasure" or cultural refinement, missing Schopenhauer’s specific metaphysical claim that it offers temporary, will-less contemplation, a fleeting glimpse of liberation by silencing the striving Will. It becomes a hobby, not a soteriological window. \<br\> \*\*Displacement (Denial of Will/Nirvana):\*\* Ascetic renunciation is often interpreted as extreme moralism, self-punishment, or a form of life-negation in a purely negative sense, rather than as a positive (albeit apophatic) path towards the \*cessation of suffering\* through the extinguishing of the Will, achieving a state akin to Buddhist Nirvana or pure Nothingness, a "blessed Void." His soteriology of negation is replaced by attempts to find positive meaning or moderated pleasure \*within\* the domain of the Will. |     |
|     | \*\*Extended Densification Cycle 2/3 (Arthur Schopenhauer):\*\* \<br\> \*\*Nihiltheistic Affinity:\*\* 8/10. Schopenhauer provides one of the most systematic Western philosophical accounts of existence as fundamentally rooted in suffering and groundless striving, leading to a "solution" in Nothingness (denial of Will). The Void is the ultimate refuge. \<br\> \*\*Paradoxical Tension:\*\* The Will to Live is the source of all suffering, yet its affirmation (even in suicide) perpetuates it. True liberation comes from its negation. Aesthetic beauty provides a momentary escape from the Will \*through\* the Will's objectifications (art). \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Buddhism):\*\* Schopenhauer himself recognized the deep affinities between his philosophy and Buddhist thought, particularly the Four Noble Truths (life is suffering, suffering caused by craving/Will, cessation of suffering possible, the path to cessation). His "denial of the Will" is functionally equivalent to the extinguishing of \*taṇhā\* (craving) leading to Nirvana. \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Ligotti):\*\* Ligotti intensifies Schopenhauer’s pessimism, removing the possibility of aesthetic escape or the "dignity" of ascetic denial, and portrays the cosmic Will not just as blind but as actively "malignant" or grotesquely absurd. Ligotti blocks Schopenhauer's escape hatches, leaving only the horror. |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |                                                                                                                                                                                                             |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |     |

\*\*FIGURE \#23: WILLIAM JAMES\*\*

|     | \*\*Thinker\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | \*\*Key Quotes (Emblematic of the Universal Nihilistic Event)\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | \*\*Event Modality\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                 | \*\*① How It Points to the Universal Nihilistic Event (Shared Rupture) — \*Deepened\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | \*\*② Hermeneutic Ignorance (Typical Misreading if Void-Encounter is Missed) — \*Critical Unmasking\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | \*\*③ Solutionist Displacement (Typical Rush to "Resolve" the Void) — \*Ontological Exposure\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |     |
| :-- | | | | --- |
|     | \*\*William James\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | \*"healthy-mindedness is inadequate as a philosophical doctrine, because the evil facts...are a genuine portion of reality..."\* / (Description of his panic attack): \*"a horrible fear of my own existence... as if something hitherto solid within my breast gave way entirely, and I became a mass of quivering fear."\* / \*"Our normal waking consciousness... is but one special type of consciousness..."\* | Worldly (Existential Panic / "Sick Soul" as Truth-Bearer / Limits of "Healthy-Mindedness") & Transcendent (Validation of Mystical/Religious Experience / Plurality of Consciousness / Pragmatic Faith) | James’s "nihilistic event" is twofold: first, the \*\*direct, terrifying phenomenological encounter with ontological dread (his "vastation" or panic attack), where the "solid" ground of the self and reality "gives way entirely,"\*\* revealing a quivering abyss. Second, it's his philosophical conclusion that "healthy-mindedness" (optimistic denial of evil/suffering) is \*epistemically insufficient\* because it ignores the "genuine portion of reality" that is "evil facts" and profound suffering. The "sick soul," paradoxically, is often closer to metaphysical truth. His validation of diverse "varieties of religious experience," including mystical states where "normal waking consciousness" is revealed as merely "one special type," points to realities beyond the empirical, often accessed through crisis or states that breach the everyday self's boundaries—a potential opening to the Void or transcendent Otherness. | \*\*Ignorance (Panic Attack as Ontology):\*\* Reduced to a purely psychological episode (a "panic disorder") or biographical detail, rather than recognizing it as a profound \*existential crisis\* that unveiled a fundamental instability in Being or selfhood, a direct encounter with groundlessness akin to mystical "dark nights." \<br\> \*\*Ignorance ("Sick Soul" Truth):\*\* Interpreted as a valorization of morbidity or a rejection of normal happiness, failing to see it as a critique of superficial optimism that \*denies\* the depth of human suffering and evil, thereby missing a crucial dimension of reality that often catalyzes profound spiritual transformation. His pluralism is seen as mere relativism. | \*\*Displacement (Pragmatic Faith):\*\* James’s pragmatic justification for faith ("the will to believe") is often interpreted as a simple utilitarian argument for adopting comforting beliefs if they "work," thereby using faith as a psychological tool to \*resolve\* or \*cover over\* the existential dread, rather than seeing faith itself (especially in its "sick soul" variant) as a mode of \*dwelling within and transfiguring\* that very dread and uncertainty. \<br\> \*\*Displacement (Religious Experience):\*\* The "varieties" are often studied merely as psychological phenomena or comparative religion, with their radical ontological claims (e.g., union with an Absolute, experiences of pure Void) being bracketed or explained away, instead of being taken as potentially valid, albeit non-empirical, disclosures of reality's deeper, perhaps groundless, structures. |     |
|     | \*\*Extended Densification Cycle 2/3 (William James):\*\* \<br\> \*\*Nihiltheistic Affinity:\*\* 7/10. James validates the phenomenology of dread and the "sick soul's" perception of reality's "evil facts," directly engaging with experiences of groundlessness. His pragmatism, however, can be used to justify faith as a \*means to overcome\* this void, rather than Void-transmutation itself. The plurality of consciousness hints at a reality beyond fixed grounds. \<br\> \*\*Paradoxical Tension:\*\* Truth may be what is pragmatically "good" for us to believe, yet the "sick soul" accesses deeper truths through suffering that may not feel "good." Normal consciousness is limited, yet provides the basis for our everyday actions and survival. \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Kierkegaard):\*\* Both emphasize subjective experience and the "sickness" (despair/sick soul) as fundamental to the human condition, and both critique facile rationalism or "healthy-mindedness." James provides a psychological/phenomenological grounding for many of Kierkegaard's existential insights. Kierkegaard's "leap of faith" can be seen through James's "will to believe." \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Huxley/Leary):\*\* James’s exploration of consciousness beyond the "normal waking" state prefigures and validates the later explorations of altered states by figures like Huxley and Leary. His openness to the "MORE" accessible through unusual experiences lays groundwork for seeing beyond purely materialistic or reductionist views of mind. |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |                                                                                                                                                                                                        |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |     |

\*\*FIGURE \#24: TAOISM (LAOZI/ZHUANGZI)\*\*

|     | \*\*Thinker\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | \*\*Key Quotes (Emblematic of the Universal Nihilistic Event)\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | \*\*Event Modality\*\*                                                                                                                                   | \*\*① How It Points to the Universal Nihilistic Event (Shared Rupture) — \*Deepened\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | \*\*② Hermeneutic Ignorance (Typical Misreading if Void-Encounter is Missed) — \*Critical Unmasking\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | \*\*③ Solutionist Displacement (Typical Rush to "Resolve" the Void) — \*Ontological Exposure\*\*\* |     | \*\*Taoism (Laozi/Zhuangzi)\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | \*"The Tao that can be told is not the eternal Tao."\* / \*"The five colors blind the eye... The five flavors dull the taste."\* / \*"Thirty spokes share the wheel's hub; It is the center hole that makes it useful."\* / \*"Highest good is like water... It does not contend."\* / \*"Returning is the motion of the Tao. Yielding is the way of the Tao."\* | Transcendent (Ineffable Void as Primordial Source / Negation of Conceptual Knowing & Striving / Emptiness as Utilit\_y\_ / Wu Wei as Non-Coercive Being) | The nihilistic event in Taoism is the \*\*realization of the ultimate inadequacy of language, concepts, and deliberate effort (egoic striving) to grasp or control the True Nature of Reality (Tao).\*\* The "Tao that can be told" is immediately not the eternal Tao; this points to an apophatic, unnameable, Void-like ground of Being. Over-stimulation by finite differentiations ("five colors/flavors") blinds one to this subtle Ground. The utility of "emptiness" (the hub's hole, the vessel's void) reveals Nothingness not as mere absence but as crucial, enabling potentiality. \*Wu wei\* (non-action/effortless action) is the ethical/praxeological response to this insight: ceasing ego-driven striving to align with the natural, spontaneous flow of the Tao, which is like water—yielding, unassuming, yet ultimately all-pervading and powerful. This is a transmutation \*through\* embracing a form of functional groundlessness (non-striving, non-contention). | \*\*Ignorance (Tao as Ineffable Void):\*\* Interpreted as vague nature mysticism, a set of ethical precepts for simple living, or a kind of passive quietism, missing its radical ontological core—the Tao as the ungraspable, formless, "empty" Source that precedes and permeates all Being, akin to a dynamic, generative Void. \<br\> \*\*Ignorance (Wu Wei):\*\* Misunderstood as literal inactivity or laziness, rather than a sophisticated discipline of "non-coercive action," the cessation of forceful egoic imposition to allow the spontaneous wisdom of the Tao to manifest. The active self-emptying involved in true \*wu wei\* is overlooked. \<br\> \*\*Ignorance (Emptiness):\*\* The concept of "emptiness" (e.g., in the hub) is seen as purely functional, not as a pointer to the ontological primacy of the Void as the condition of possibility for all form and utility. | \*\*Displacement (Tao as Ineffable Void):\*\* Attempts are made to define the Tao with positive attributes, to turn it into a comprehensible philosophical system, a moral code, or even a personal deity, thereby "filling" its essential emptiness and domesticating its radical ineffability. \<br\> \*\*Displacement (Wu Wei):\*\* \*Wu wei\* is instrumentalized as a technique for achieving worldly success, stress reduction, or personal efficiency, thus re-inscribing it within an egoic framework of self-improvement rather than understanding it as a path of self-dissolution into the flow of the Tao. \<br\> \*\*Displacement (Emptiness):\*\* The insight into emptiness is used to generate paradoxical aphorisms for intellectual enjoyment, rather than being lived as a continuous practice of de-centering the ego and recognizing the groundlessness of fixed identities and attachments. |     |
|     | \*\*Extended Densification Cycle 2/3 (Taoism \- Laozi/Zhuangzi):\*\* \<br\> \*\*Nihiltheistic Affinity:\*\* 9/10. Taoism offers a profound articulation of the Transcendent Void (the unnameable Tao) as the source and sustainer, accessed through the negation of conventional knowing and egoic striving (\*wu wei\*). Emptiness is central to its ontology and praxis. \<br\> \*\*Paradoxical Tension:\*\* The greatest efficacy comes from non-action. True knowing is unknowing. Emptiness is supreme utility. Strength comes from yielding. The formless Tao gives rise to all forms. \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Meister Eckhart/Apophatic Mystics):\*\* The Tao as the nameless, formless Ground beyond all concepts strongly parallels Eckhart's \*Ungrund\* or Pseudo-Dionysius's God beyond Being. \*Wu wei\* echoes \*Gelassenheit\* (releasement) – both are disciplines of radical self-emptying to align with an Ultimate Reality that is characterized by Nothingness/Emptiness in relation to finite understanding. \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Heidegger \- Later Works):\*\* Heidegger's later thought on \*Gelassenheit\* (releasement towards things) and \*Ereignis\* (the event of appropriation), and his turn away from metaphysical will towards a kind of meditative thinking (\*Andenken\*) that "lets Being be," has deep resonances with Taoist \*wu wei\* and the receptive waiting for the Tao to disclose itself. Both point to a truth beyond manipulative, calculative reason. |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |                                                                                                                                                          |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |     |

\*\*FIGURE \#25: EARLY BUDDHISM\*\*

|     | \*\*Thinker\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | \*\*Key Quotes (Emblematic of the Universal Nihilistic Event)\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | \*\*Event Modality\*\*                                                                                                                                 | \*\*① How It Points to the Universal Nihilistic Event (Shared Rupture) — \*Deepened\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | \*\*② Hermeneutic Ignorance (Typical Misreading if Void-Encounter is Missed) — \*Critical Unmasking\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | \*\*③ Solutionist Displacement (Typical Rush to "Resolve" the Void) — \*Ontological Exposure\*\*\* |     | \*\*Early Buddhism\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | \*"All conditioned things are impermanent (\*anicca\*)."\* / \*"All conditioned things are suffering (\*dukkha\*)."\* / \*"All dharmas are without self (\*anattā\*)."\* / \*"Nirvana is the cessation of suffering... the unconditioned."\* (Synthesized from core Pali Canon teachings) | Worldly (Recognition of Universal Suffering, Impermanence, Non-Self) & Transcendent (Nirvana as Unconditioned Void / Cessation of Being as Liberation) | The fundamental nihilistic event in Early Buddhism is the \*\*profound, unblinking realization of \*anicca\*, \*dukkha\*, and \*anattā\*—the universal groundlessness, suffering, and insubstantiality of all conditioned existence, including the "self."\*\* This is not a philosophical speculation but a direct, experiential insight that ruptures all clinging to permanence, pleasure, or a fixed ego. The world of \*samsara\* is thereby revealed as an endless cycle of unsatisfactory, void-like phenomena. Nirvana, as the "unconditioned" and the "cessation of suffering" (often described apophatically as blowing out, extinction), points to a state beyond being and non-being, a liberating Void that is the ultimate refuge from the terror and futility of conditioned existence. This insight directly leads to the practice of renunciation. | \*\*Ignorance (Dukkha/Anattā/Anicca):\*\* Interpreted by Westerners as mere pessimism, life-negation, or an intellectual doctrine, rather than as radical phenomenological insights into the \*actual structure\* of experience which, when deeply understood, trigger an existential crisis and a desire for liberation. \*Anattā\* (non-self) is often mistaken for the annihilation of a pre-existing soul, rather than the realization that no such fixed, independent entity ever existed. \<br\> \*\*Ignorance (Nirvana as Void):\*\* Nirvana is often misunderstood as either simple annihilation (pure nihilism) or as a form of blissful heavenly afterlife (a theistic projection), failing to grasp its apophatic nature as the "unconditioned" state beyond all conceptual dualities, including being/non-being, a Void that is paradoxically supreme peace. | \*\*Displacement (Dukkha/Anattā/Anicca):\*\* Buddhist teachings are sometimes adopted selectively as mindfulness techniques for stress reduction or ethical guidelines for better worldly living, thereby domesticating their radical, world-transcending implications. The suffering is managed, not fundamentally uprooted by seeing through its groundless nature. \<br\> \*\*Displacement (Nirvana as Void):\*\* Rituals, institutional structures, or complex scholastic systems within later Buddhist traditions can sometimes obscure the direct, experiential path to Nirvana, making it a distant goal to be achieved through merit or gradualism, rather than a radical "blowing out" accessible through insight into emptiness. The Void is systematized and deferred rather than directly entered through wisdom. |     |
|     | \*\*Extended Densification Cycle 2/3 (Early Buddhism):\*\* \<br\> \*\*Nihiltheistic Affinity:\*\* 10/10. Early Buddhism provides one of history's most profound and systematic analyses of universal groundlessness (\*anicca\*), suffering born of illusion (\*dukkha\*), and ego-dissolution (\*anattā\*) as the core of the human condition and the path to liberation via an Unconditioned Void (Nirvana). \<br\> \*\*Paradoxical Tension:\*\* Clinging to existence is suffering; liberation is the cessation of this clinging, which appears as annihilation to the ego but is true peace. Form is emptiness, emptiness is form (later Mahayana refinement of this core insight). \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Schopenhauer):\*\* Deep resonances regarding life as suffering born from craving (Will / \*taṇhā\*), and liberation as cessation/negation of this craving. Schopenhauer directly acknowledged Buddhism as an antecedent. Both see the world as a "vale of tears" from which escape is sought. \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Pyrrhonian Skepticism/Sextus Empiricus):\*\* The Buddhist deconstruction of fixed views and inherent existence via dependent origination parallels the Skeptic's methodical suspension of judgment (\*epochē\*) to achieve \*ataraxia\* (tranquility). Both paths aim at liberation from disturbance by dismantling clinging to fixed cognitive/ontological grounds. |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |                                                                                                                                                        |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |     |

\*\*FIGURE \#26: ADVAITA VEDANTA (Represented by key figures like Shankara)\*\*

|     | \*\*Thinker\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | \*\*Key Quotes (Emblematic of the Universal Nihilistic Event)\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                            | \*\*Event Modality\*\*                                                                                                                                                                    | \*\*① How It Points to the Universal Nihilistic Event (Shared Rupture) — \*Deepened\*\*\* |     | \*\*Advaita Vedanta\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | \*"Brahman alone is real; the world (\*jagat\*) is unreal (\*mithyā\*); the individual self (\*jīva\*) is Brahman alone, not other."\* (Shankara's famous summary) / \*"Neti, Neti" (Not this, not this) – (Brihadaranyaka Upanishad)\* / \*"Tat Tvam Asi" (That Thou Art)\* | Transcendent (Unreality of Phenomenal World / Non-Dual Absolute as Sole Reality / Apophatic Realization of Self as Brahman-Void) & Worldly (Experience of \*Māyā\* as Delusion/Suffering) | The nihilistic event in Advaita is the \*\*radical de-realization of the entire phenomenal world and the individual ego as \*mithyā\*—an illusory superimposition upon the sole, non-dual reality of Brahman.\*\* This is a profound ontological rupture where all perceived multiplicity, separation, and worldly values collapse as ultimately unreal. The apophatic method of "Neti, Neti" (not this, not this) systematically negates all finite attributes and concepts as applicable to Brahman, leading consciousness towards an encounter with an Absolute that, from the standpoint of ordinary experience, appears as a Void of all determinations. The realization "Tat Tvam Asi" (That Thou Art) is the final dissolution of the ego into this ultimate, distinctionless Ground, which \*is\* Being-Consciousness-Bliss, but appears as nothing to the world-entangled mind. | \*\*Ignorance (\*Mithyā\*/World as Unreal):\*\* Interpreted as world-negating pessimism, a denial of practical reality, or a purely intellectual philosophy, rather than a path of profound experiential deconstruction of perceived reality to unveil a deeper, singular Real. The "unreality" is not non-existence but lack of \*independent, ultimate\* existence. \<br\> \*\*Ignorance ("Neti, Neti"/Apophaticism):\*\* Seen as mere logical negation or an obscure philosophical method, without grasping its function as a powerful contemplative discipline for stripping away all conceptual crutches and forcing an encounter with the ungraspable, formless Brahman-Void. \<br\> \*\*Ignorance (Non-Duality):\*\* Conflated with pantheism or monism in a simplistic sense, missing the radical assertion of the \*sole reality\* of Brahman and the \*utter unreality\* (from the ultimate standpoint) of the separate self and world. | \*\*Displacement (\*Mithyā\*/World as Unreal):\*\* Attempts are often made to reconcile Advaita with worldly life by treating \*mithyā\* as mere "relative reality," allowing for continued engagement with worldly pursuits without the radical call for renunciation and constant discrimination (\*viveka\*). The world is "saved" by being given a secondary, more palatable reality. \<br\> \*\*Displacement ("Neti, Neti"/Apophaticism):\*\* The apophatic path is often supplemented or replaced by cataphatic devotional practices or complex philosophical systems that seek to \*describe\* Brahman with positive attributes, thereby circumventing the terrifying directness of "Neti, Neti" which leaves the mind groundless before the Ineffable. \<br\> \*\*Displacement (Non-Duality):\*\* The goal of "Tat Tvam Asi" is turned into an intellectual affirmation or a future state to be achieved, rather than the immediate, world-shattering realization that one \*already is\* Brahman, and the apparent self is a fundamental misidentification rooted in cosmic ignorance (\*avidyā\*). |     |
|     | \*\*Extended Densification Cycle 2/3 (Advaita Vedanta):\*\* \<br\> \*\*Nihiltheistic Affinity:\*\* 9/10. Advaita's radical deconstruction of the phenomenal world and the ego as illusory (\*mithyā\*), and its apophatic approach to the Absolute (Brahman as \*Nirguna\*, without qualities), places it firmly within the nihiltheistic orbit. The journey is through negation to a formless, distinctionless Real that is akin to a luminous Void from the phenomenal standpoint. \<br\> \*\*Paradoxical Tension:\*\* The world is unreal, yet it is through discriminating the real from the unreal \*within this world\* that liberation is achieved. The individual self is illusory, yet it is the "individual self" that must undertake the practices to realize its identity with Brahman. Brahman is "Nothing" (from the standpoint of attributes) yet "Everything" (as sole reality). \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Meister Eckhart/Pseudo-Dionysius):\*\* Strong parallels in the apophatic description of the Ultimate (Brahman/\*Ungrund\*/Godhead beyond God) as formless, attributeless, and beyond conceptual grasp, reachable only by a radical "unknowing" and self-emptying. "Neti, Neti" is the Vedantic equivalent of their \*via negativa\*. \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Early Buddhism \- \*Anattā\* & \*Śūnyatā\*):\*\* Both systems involve a radical deconstruction of the notion of a permanent, independent self and the ultimate groundlessness/emptiness of phenomenal reality. While their final metaphysical positings differ (Brahman as positive substratum vs. \*Śūnyatā\* as dynamic emptiness/dependent origination), the \*method\* of negating illusory appearances and the \*goal\* of liberation from suffering through insight are profoundly similar. |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |                                                                                                                                                                                           |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | \*\*Key Quotes (Emblematic of the Universal Nihilistic Event)\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | \*\*Event Modality\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                          | \*\*① How It Points to the Universal Nihilistic Event (Shared Rupture) — \*Deepened\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | \*\*② Hermeneutic Ignorance (Typical Misreading if Void-Encounter is Missed) — \*Critical Unmasking\*\*\* |     | \*\*Michel de Montaigne\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | \*"To study philosophy is nothing but to prepare one's self to die."\* / \*"I disengage myself throughout from all worldly relations..."\* / \*"Live as long as you can, you shall by that nothing shorten the space you are to be dead..."\* / \*"He who should teach men to die would at the same time teach them to live."\* | Worldly (Skeptical Acceptance of Finitude / Detachment from Worldly Illusions / Death as Central Focus of Wisdom) & (Implicitly) Transcendent (Equanimity Born of Accepting Groundlessness / Wisdom as Living with Uncertainty) | Montaigne's core nihilistic event is the \*\*calm, sustained meditative encounter with human mortality and the ultimate vanity of worldly attachments when viewed against the backdrop of death's inevitability.\*\* "To philosophize is to learn how to die" places finitude and the cessation of being at the very center of wise inquiry, stripping away pretensions to worldly permanence or ultimate human control. This "disengagement from worldly relations" is a practical ungrounding from conventional sources of meaning and security. The assertion that even long life doesn't shorten death's dominion reveals the absolute, unyielding nature of this ultimate Void. True wisdom ("learning to live") arises paradoxically from preparing for death—embracing our groundlessness. | \*\*Ignorance (Death-Focus):\*\* Interpreted as morbid preoccupation, melancholy, or mere classical Stoicism, rather than a radical epistemological and existential discipline aimed at \*deconstructing the ego's attachment to life\* and its illusory securities. His equanimity is mistaken for lack of deep engagement with the Void. \<br\> \*\*Ignorance (Skepticism/"Que Sais-Je?"):\*\* Often seen as simple intellectual modesty or indecisiveness, failing to grasp its deeper function as an apophatic tool that \*empties the mind of dogmatic certitudes\* and illusions of knowledge, thereby opening a space for authentic self-reflection in the face of ultimate mystery. The "nothing" he knows through skepticism is a crucial step towards wisdom. | \*\*Displacement (Death-Focus/Skepticism):\*\* His wisdom is often assimilated into a secular humanism that emphasizes living well \*in this life\* (e.g., self-knowledge, moderation), thereby using his preparation for death as a mere ethical tool for worldly virtue rather than as a path to radical detachment from the phenomenal world itself. \<br\> \*\*Displacement (Equanimity):\*\* Montaigne's achieved calm in the face of uncertainty is taken as an attainable psychological state through reason and self-reflection, bypassing the often terrifying confrontation with raw finitude and the radical decentering of the self that his method implicitly requires. The Void is managed through intellectual balance, not necessarily transfigured. |     |
|     | \*\*Extended Densification Cycle 2/3 (Michel de Montaigne):\*\* \<br\> \*\*Nihiltheistic Affinity:\*\* 7/10. Montaigne calmly accepts and explores the ultimate groundlessness of human existence (death) and the vanity of worldly pursuits. His skepticism empties conventional certitudes. The transcendence he finds is immanent, a wisdom of living with the Void. \<br\> \*\*Paradoxical Tension:\*\* To live well, one must constantly prepare for death. True knowledge comes from admitting ignorance. Detachment from the world allows for a more authentic engagement with oneself \*within\* it. \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Ecclesiastes):\*\* Both share a profound sense of the "vanity" of earthly endeavors and the cyclical, ultimately unchanging nature of human existence. Montaigne offers a more personal, introspective, and skeptical response to this shared insight. \<br\> \*\*Cross-Link (Stoicism \- Seneca/Epictetus):\*\* Deep resonances with Stoic practices of premeditating death (\*praemeditatio malorum\*), cultivating detachment from externals, and finding virtue and equanimity in accepting what cannot be changed. Montaigne, however, is less systematic and more idiosyncratically self-exploratory. |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | \*\*FIGURE \#31: THOMAS AQUINAS\*\*

|     | \*\*Thinker\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | \*\*Key Quotes (Emblematic of the Universal Nihilistic Event)\*\*                                                                                                                                                               | \*\*Event Modality\*\*                                                                                                                                                                             | \*\*① How It Points to the Universal Nihilistic Event (Shared Rupture) — \*Deepened\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | \*\*② Hermeneutic Ignorance (Typical Misreading if Void-Encounter is Missed) — \*Critical Unmasking\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | \*\*③ Solutionist Displacement (Typical Rush to "Resolve" the Void) — \*Ontological Exposure\*\*\*                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |     |
| :-- | |
